1.  **Increase Hydrogen Bonding:** Introduce more hydroxyl (-OH) or amine (-NH2) groups to form more hydrogen bonds with the protein. This is often the most effective way to improve affinity.
2.  **Optimize Hydrophobic Interactions:** Modify the aromatic ring or add alkyl groups to enhance hydrophobic interactions within the binding pocket.
3.  **Introduce a charged group:** Add a charged group like a deprotonated carboxylic acid (carboxylate) or a protonated amine if there's a complementary charge in the binding site.
4.  **Increase Ring Rigidity:** Fusing rings can sometimes lock the molecule into a favorable conformation for binding.
5.  **Increase size:** Assuming there is space in the pocket, adding groups to the molecule to take up additional volume may increase binding affinity through Van Der Waals forces.
